      </div>
      <h3 id="Schema-Building" data-reactid="1983">Schema Building:</h3>
      <div id="Schema-dropColumn" data-reactid="1984">
       <b data-reactid="1985">dropColumn</b>
       <!-- react-text: 1986 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="1987">table.dropColumn(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="1988">Drops a column, specified by the column's name</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-dropColumns" data-reactid="1989">
       <b data-reactid="1990">dropColumns</b>
       <!-- react-text: 1991 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="1992">table.dropColumns(*columns)</code>
       <p data-reactid="1993">Drops multiple columns, taking a variable number of column names.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-renameColumn" data-reactid="1994">
       <b data-reactid="1995">renameColumn</b>
       <!-- react-text: 1996 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="1997">table.renameColumn(from, to)</code>
       <p data-reactid="1998">Renames a column from one name to another.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-increments" data-reactid="1999">
       <b data-reactid="2000">increments</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2001 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2002">table.increments(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2003">Adds an auto incrementing column, in PostgreSQL this is a serial. This will be used as the primary key for the table. Also available is a bigIncrements if you wish to add a bigint incrementing number (in PostgreSQL bigserial).</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-integer" data-reactid="2004">
       <b data-reactid="2005">integer</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2006 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2007">table.integer(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2008">Adds an integer column.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-bigInteger" data-reactid="2009">
       <b data-reactid="2010">bigInteger</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2011 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2012">table.bigInteger(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2013">In MySQL or PostgreSQL, adds a bigint column, otherwise adds a normal integer. Note that bigint data is returned as a string in queries because JavaScript may be unable to parse them without loss of precision.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-text" data-reactid="2014">
       <b data-reactid="2015">text</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2016 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2017">table.text(name, [textType])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2018">Adds a text column, with optional textType for MySql text datatype preference. textType may be mediumtext or longtext, otherwise defaults to text.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-string" data-reactid="2019">
       <b data-reactid="2020">string</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2021 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2022">table.string(name, [length])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2023">Adds a string column, with optional length defaulting to 255.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-float" data-reactid="2024">
       <b data-reactid="2025">float</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2026 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2027">table.float(column, [precision], [scale])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2028">Adds a float column, with optional precision (defaults to 8) and scale (defaults to 2).</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-decimal" data-reactid="2029">
       <b data-reactid="2030">decimal</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2031 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2032">table.decimal(column, [precision], [scale])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2033">Adds a decimal column, with optional precision (defaults to 8) and scale (defaults to 2).</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-boolean" data-reactid="2034">
       <b data-reactid="2035">boolean</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2036 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2037">table.boolean(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2038">Adds a boolean column.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-date" data-reactid="2039">
       <b data-reactid="2040">date</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2041 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2042">table.date(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2043">Adds a date column.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-dateTime" data-reactid="2044">
       <b data-reactid="2045">dateTime</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2046 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2047">table.dateTime(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2048">Adds a dateTime column.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-time" data-reactid="2049">
       <b data-reactid="2050">time</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2051 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2052">table.time(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2053">Adds a time column.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-timestamp" data-reactid="2054">
       <b data-reactid="2055">timestamp</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2056 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2057">table.timestamp(name, [standard])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2058">Adds a timestamp column, defaults to timestamptz in PostgreSQL, unless true is passed as the second argument. For Example:</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2059"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2060">table.timestamp(<span class="hljs-string">'created_at'</span>).defaultTo(knex.fn.now());</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-timestamps" data-reactid="2061">
       <b data-reactid="2062">timestamps</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2063 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2064">table.timestamps([useTimestamps], [defaultToNow])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2065">Adds a created_at and updated_at column on the database, setting these each to dateTime types. When true is passed as the first argument a timestamp type is used. Both colums default to being not null and the current timestamp when true is passed as the second argument.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-dropTimestamps" data-reactid="2066">
       <b data-reactid="2067">dropTimestamps</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2068 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2069">table.dropTimestamps()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2070">Drops the columns created_at and updated_at from the table, which can be created via timestamps.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-binary" data-reactid="2071">
       <b data-reactid="2072">binary</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2073 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2074">table.binary(name, [length])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2075">Adds a binary column, with optional length argument for MySQL.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-enum / enu" data-reactid="2076">
       <b data-reactid="2077">enum / enu</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2078 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2079">table.enu(col, values)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2080">Adds a enum column, (aliased to enu, as enum is a reserved word in JavaScript). Note that the second argument is an array of values. Example:</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2081"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2082">table.enu(<span class="hljs-string">'column'</span>, [<span class="hljs-string">'value1'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'value2'</span>])</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-json" data-reactid="2083">
       <b data-reactid="2084">json</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2085 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2086">table.json(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2087">Adds a json column, using the built-in json type in postgresql, defaulting to a text column in older versions of postgresql or in unsupported databases. Note that when setting an array (or a value that could be an array) as the value of a json or jsonb column, you should use JSON.stringify() to convert your value to a string prior to passing it to the query builder, e.g.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2088"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2089">knex.table(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.where({<span class="hljs-attr">id</span>: <span class="hljs-number">1</span>})
.update({<span class="hljs-attr">json_data</span>: <span class="hljs-built_in">JSON</span>.stringify(mightBeAnArray)});</code></pre>
       <p data-reactid="2090">This is because postgresql has a native array type which uses a syntax incompatible with json; knex has no way of knowing which syntax to use, and calling JSON.stringify() forces json-style syntax.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-jsonb" data-reactid="2091">
       <b data-reactid="2092">jsonb</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2093 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2094">table.jsonb(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2095">Adds a jsonb column. Works similar to table.json(), but uses native jsonb type if possible.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-uuid" data-reactid="2096">
       <b data-reactid="2097">uuid</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2098 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2099">table.uuid(name)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2100">Adds a uuid column - this uses the built-in uuid type in postgresql, and falling back to a char(36) in other databases.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-comment" data-reactid="2101">
       <b data-reactid="2102">comment</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2103 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2104">table.comment(value)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2105">Sets the comment for a table.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-engine" data-reactid="2106">
       <b data-reactid="2107">engine</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2108 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2109">table.engine(val)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2110">Sets the engine for the database table, only available within a createTable call, and only applicable to MySQL.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-charset" data-reactid="2111">
       <b data-reactid="2112">charset</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2113 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2114">table.charset(val)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2115">Sets the charset for the database table, only available within a createTable call, and only applicable to MySQL.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-collate" data-reactid="2116">
       <b data-reactid="2117">collate</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2118 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2119">table.collate(val)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2120">Sets the collation for the database table, only available within a createTable call, and only applicable to MySQL.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-inherits" data-reactid="2121">
       <b data-reactid="2122">inherits</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2123 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2124">table.inherits(val)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2125">Sets the tables that this table inherits, only available within a createTable call, and only applicable to PostgreSQL.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-specificType" data-reactid="2126">
       <b data-reactid="2127">specificType</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2128 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2129">table.specificType(column, value)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2130">Sets a specific type for the column creation, if you'd like to add a column type that isn't supported here.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-index" data-reactid="2131">
       <b data-reactid="2132">index</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2133 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2134">table.index(columns, [indexName], [indexType])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2135">Adds an index to a table over the given columns. A default index name using the columns is used unless indexName is specified. The indexType can be optionally specified for PostgreSQL.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-dropIndex" data-reactid="2136">
       <b data-reactid="2137">dropIndex</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2138 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2139">table.dropIndex(columns, [indexName])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2140">Drops an index from a table. A default index name using the columns is used unless indexName is specified (in which case columns is ignored).</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-unique" data-reactid="2141">
       <b data-reactid="2142">unique</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2143 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2144">table.unique(columns)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2145">Adds an unique index to a table over the given <code>columns</code></p>
       <pre data-reactid="2146"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2147">knex.schema.alterTable(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>, <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">t</span>) </span>{
  t.unique(<span class="hljs-string">'email'</span>)
})
knex.schema.alterTable(<span class="hljs-string">'job'</span>, <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">t</span>) </span>{
  t.unique([<span class="hljs-string">'account_id'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'program_id'</span>])
})</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-foreign" data-reactid="2148">
       <b data-reactid="2149">foreign</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2150 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2151">table.foreign(columns)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2152">Adds a foreign key constraint to a table for an existing column using <code>table.foreign(column).references(column)</code> or multiple columns using <code>table.foreign(columns).references(columns)</code>. You can also chain onDelete and/or onUpdate to set the reference option (RESTRICT, CASCADE, SET NULL, NO ACTION) for the operation. Note, this is the same as column.references(column) but works for existing columns.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2153"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2154">knex.schema.table(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>, <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span> (<span class="hljs-params">table</span>) </span>{
  table.integer(<span class="hljs-string">'user_id'</span>).unsigned()
  table.foreign(<span class="hljs-string">'user_id'</span>).references(<span class="hljs-string">'Items.user_id_in_items'</span>)
})</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-dropForeign" data-reactid="2155">
       <b data-reactid="2156">dropForeign</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2157 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2158">table.dropForeign(columns, [foreignKeyName])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2159">Drops a foreign key constraint from a table. A default foreign key name using the columns is used unless foreignKeyName is specified (in which case columns is ignored).</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-dropUnique" data-reactid="2160">
       <b data-reactid="2161">dropUnique</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2162 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2163">table.dropUnique(columns, [indexName])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2164">Drops a unique key constraint from a table. A default unique key name using the columns is used unless indexName is specified (in which case columns is ignored).</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-dropPrimary" data-reactid="2165">
       <b data-reactid="2166">dropPrimary</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2167 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2168">table.dropPrimary([constraintName])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2169">Drops the primary key constraint on a table. Defaults to tablename_pkey unless constraintName is specified.</p>
      </div>
      <h3 id="Chainable" data-reactid="2170">Chainable Methods:</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2171">The following three methods may be chained on the schema building methods, as modifiers to the column.</p>
      <div id="Schema-alter" data-reactid="2172">
       <b data-reactid="2173">alter</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2174 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2175">column.alter()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2176">Marks the column as an alter / modify, instead of the default add. Note: This only works in .alterTable() and is not supported by SQlite. Alter is <em>not</em> done incrementally over older column type so if you like to add <code>notNull</code> and keep the old default value, the alter statement must contain both <code>.notNull().defaultTo(1).alter()</code>. If one just tries to add <code>.notNull().alter()</code> the old default value will be dropped.</p>
      </div>
      <pre data-reactid="2177"><code data-reactid="2178">knex.schema.alterTable('user', function(t) {
  t.increments().primary(); // add
  // drops previous default value from column, change type to string and add not nullable constraint
  t.string('username', 35).notNullable().alter(); 
  // drops both not null contraint and the default value
  t.integer('age').alter(); 
});</code></pre>
      <div id="Schema-index" data-reactid="2179">
       <b data-reactid="2180">index</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2181 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2182">column.index([indexName], [indexType])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2183">Specifies a field as an index. If an indexName is specified, it is used in place of the standard index naming convention of tableName_columnName. The indexType can be optionally specified for PostgreSQL. No-op if this is chained off of a field that cannot be indexed.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-primary" data-reactid="2184">
       <b data-reactid="2185">primary</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2186 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2187">column.primary([constraintName])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2188"></p>
       <pre><code>  When called on a single column it will set that column as the primary key for a table.
  To create a compound primary key, pass an array of column names:
  `table.primary(['column1', 'column2'])`.
  Constraint name defaults to `tablename_pkey` unless `constraintName` is specified.
</code></pre>
       <p></p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-unique" data-reactid="2189">
       <b data-reactid="2190">unique</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2191 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2192">column.unique()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2193">Sets the column as unique.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-references" data-reactid="2194">
       <b data-reactid="2195">references</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2196 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2197">column.references(column)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2198">Sets the "column" that the current column references as a foreign key. "column" can either be ".
        <column>
         " syntax, or just the column name followed up with a call to inTable to specify the table.
        </column></p>
       <table></table>
       <p></p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-inTable" data-reactid="2199">
       <b data-reactid="2200">inTable</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2201 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2202">column.inTable(table)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2203">Sets the "table" where the foreign key column is located after calling column.references.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-onDelete" data-reactid="2204">
       <b data-reactid="2205">onDelete</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2206 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2207">column.onDelete(command)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2208">Sets the SQL command to be run "onDelete".</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-onUpdate" data-reactid="2209">
       <b data-reactid="2210">onUpdate</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2211 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2212">column.onUpdate(command)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2213">Sets the SQL command to be run "onUpdate".</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-defaultTo" data-reactid="2214">
       <b data-reactid="2215">defaultTo</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2216 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2217">column.defaultTo(value)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2218">Sets the default value for the column on an insert.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-unsigned" data-reactid="2219">
       <b data-reactid="2220">unsigned</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2221 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2222">column.unsigned()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2223">Specifies an integer as unsigned. No-op if this is chained off of a non-integer field.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-notNullable" data-reactid="2224">
       <b data-reactid="2225">notNullable</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2226 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2227">column.notNullable()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2228">Adds a not null on the current column being created.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-nullable" data-reactid="2229">
       <b data-reactid="2230">nullable</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2231 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2232">column.nullable()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2233">Default on column creation, this explicitly sets a field to be nullable.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-first" data-reactid="2234">
       <b data-reactid="2235">first</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2236 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2237">column.first()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2238">Sets the column to be inserted on the first position, only used in MySQL alter tables.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-after" data-reactid="2239">
       <b data-reactid="2240">after</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2241 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2242">column.after(field)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2243">Sets the column to be inserted after another, only used in MySQL alter tables.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Schema-comment" data-reactid="2244">
       <b data-reactid="2245">comment</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2246 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2247">column.comment(value)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2248">Sets the comment for a column.</p>
      </div>
      <pre data-reactid="2249"><code data-reactid="2250">knex.schema.createTable('accounts', function(t) {
  t.increments().primary();
  t.string('email').unique().comment('This is the email field');
});</code></pre>
      <div id="Schema-collate" data-reactid="2251">
       <b data-reactid="2252">collate</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2253 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2254">column.collate(collation)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2255">Sets the collation for a column (only works in MySQL). Here is a list of all available collations: <a href="https://dev.mysql.com/doc/refman/5.5/en/charset-charsets.html">https://dev.mysql.com/doc/refman/5.5/en/charset-charsets.html</a></p>
      </div>
      <pre data-reactid="2256"><code data-reactid="2257">knex.schema.createTable('users', function(t) {
  t.increments();
  t.string('email').unique().collate('utf8_unicode_ci');
});</code></pre>
     </div>
     <div id="Raw" data-reactid="2258">
      <h2 id="Raw" data-reactid="2259">Raw</h2>
      <p data-reactid="2260">Sometimes you may need to use a raw expression in a query. Raw query object may be injected pretty much anywhere you want, and using proper bindings can ensure your values are escaped properly, preventing SQL-injection attacks.</p>
      <h3 id="Raw-Bindings" data-reactid="2261">Raw Parameter Binding:</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2262">One can paramterize sql given to <code>knex.raw(sql, bindings)</code>. Parameters can be positional named. One can also choose if parameter should be treated as value or as sql identifier e.g. in case of <code>'TableName.ColumnName'</code> reference.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2263"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2264">knex(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.select(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'count(*) as user_count, status'</span>))
.where(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-number">1</span>))
.orWhere(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'status &lt;&gt; ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>]))
.groupBy(<span class="hljs-string">'status'</span>)</code><br data-reactid="2265">
       <!-- react-text: 2266 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2267"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2268"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">count</span>(*) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> user_count, <span class="hljs-keyword">status</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`users`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> <span class="hljs-number">1</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">or</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">status</span> &lt;&gt; <span class="hljs-number">1</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">group</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span> <span class="hljs-string">`status`</span></code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2269">Positional bindings <code>?</code> are interpreted as values and <code>??</code> are interpreted as identifiers.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2270"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2271">knex(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).where(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'?? = ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-string">'user.name'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>]))</code><br data-reactid="2272">
       <!-- react-text: 2273 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2274"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2275"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> * <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`users`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> <span class="hljs-string">`user`</span>.<span class="hljs-string">`name`</span> = <span class="hljs-number">1</span></code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2276">Named bindings such as <code>:name</code> are interpreted as values and <code>:name:</code> interpreted as identifiers. Named bindings are processed so long as the value is anything other than <code>undefined</code>.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2277"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2278">knex(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.where(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">':name: = :thisGuy or :name: = :otherGuy or :name: = :undefinedBinding'</span>, {
  <span class="hljs-attr">name</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'users.name'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">thisGuy</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Bob'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">otherGuy</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Jay'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">undefinedBinding</span>: <span class="hljs-literal">undefined</span>
}))</code><br data-reactid="2279">
       <!-- react-text: 2280 -->Error:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2281"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2282">Undefined binding(s) detected when compiling RAW query: `users`.`name` = ? or `users`.`name` = ? or `users`.`name` = :undefinedBinding</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2283">For simpler queries where one only has a single binding, <code>.raw</code> can accept said binding as its second parameter.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2284"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2285">knex(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.where(
  knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'LOWER("login") = ?'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'knex'</span>)
)
.orWhere(
  knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'accesslevel = ?'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>)
)
.orWhere(
  knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'updtime = ?'</span>, <span class="hljs-keyword">new</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">Date</span>.UTC(<span class="hljs-string">'01-01-2016'</span>))
)</code><br data-reactid="2286">
       <!-- react-text: 2287 -->Error:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2288"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2289">Date.UTC is not a constructor</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2290">Note that due to ambiguity, arrays must be passed as arguments within a containing array.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2291"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2292">knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'select * from users where id in (?)'</span>, [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>]);
<span class="hljs-comment">// Error: Expected 3 bindings, saw 1</span>

knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'select * from users where id in (?)'</span>, [[<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>]])</code><br data-reactid="2293">
       <!-- react-text: 2294 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2295"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2296"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> * <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">users</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">id</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">in</span> (<span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-number">2</span>, <span class="hljs-number">3</span>)</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2297">To prevent replacement of <code>?</code> one can use the escape sequence <code>\\?</code>.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2298"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2299">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).where(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'='</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>).whereRaw(<span class="hljs-string">'?? \\? ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-string">'jsonColumn'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'jsonKey'</span>])</code><br data-reactid="2300">
       <!-- react-text: 2301 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2302"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2303"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> * <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`users`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> <span class="hljs-string">`id`</span> = <span class="hljs-number">1</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">and</span> <span class="hljs-string">`jsonColumn`</span> ? <span class="hljs-string">'jsonKey'</span></code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2304">To prevent replacement of named bindings one can use the escape sequence <code>\\:</code>.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2305"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2306">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).whereRaw(<span class="hljs-string">":property: = '\\:value' OR \\:property: = :value"</span>, {
  <span class="hljs-attr">property</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">value</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Bob'</span>
})</code><br data-reactid="2307">
       <!-- react-text: 2308 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2309"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2310"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> * <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`users`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> <span class="hljs-string">`name`</span> = <span class="hljs-string">':value'</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">OR</span> :property: = <span class="hljs-string">'Bob'</span></code></pre>
      <h3 id="Raw-Expressions" data-reactid="2311">Raw Expressions:</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2312">Raw expressions are created by using <code>knex.raw(sql, [bindings])</code> and passing this as a value for any value in the query chain.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2313"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2314">knex(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.select(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'count(*) as user_count, status'</span>))
.where(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-number">1</span>))
.orWhere(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'status &lt;&gt; ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>]))
.groupBy(<span class="hljs-string">'status'</span>)</code><br data-reactid="2315">
       <!-- react-text: 2316 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2317"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2318"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">count</span>(*) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> user_count, <span class="hljs-keyword">status</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`users`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> <span class="hljs-number">1</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">or</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">status</span> &lt;&gt; <span class="hljs-number">1</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">group</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">by</span> <span class="hljs-string">`status`</span></code></pre>
      <h3 id="Raw-Queries" data-reactid="2319">Raw Queries:</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2320">The <code>knex.raw</code> may also be used to build a full query and execute it, as a standard query builder query would be executed. The benefit of this is that it uses the connection pool and provides a standard interface for the different client libraries.</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2321"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2322">knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'select * from users where id = ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>]).then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">resp</span>) </span>{ ... });</code></pre>
      <p class="info" data-reactid="2323">Note that the response will be whatever the underlying sql library would typically return on a normal query, so you may need to look at the documentation for the base library the queries are executing against to determine how to handle the response.</p>
      <h3 id="Raw-queries-wrapped" data-reactid="2324">Wrapped Queries:</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2325">The raw query builder also comes with a <code>wrap</code> method, which allows wrapping the query in a value:</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2326"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2327"><span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> subcolumn = knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'select avg(salary) from employee where dept_no = e.dept_no'</span>)
.wrap(<span class="hljs-string">'('</span>, <span class="hljs-string">') avg_sal_dept'</span>);

knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'e.lastname'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'e.salary'</span>, subcolumn)
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'employee as e'</span>)
.whereRaw(<span class="hljs-string">'dept_no = e.dept_no'</span>)</code><br data-reactid="2328">
       <!-- react-text: 2329 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2330"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2331"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> <span class="hljs-string">`e`</span>.<span class="hljs-string">`lastname`</span>, <span class="hljs-string">`e`</span>.<span class="hljs-string">`salary`</span>, (<span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">avg</span>(salary) <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> employee <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> dept_no = e.dept_no) avg_sal_dept <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`employee`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> <span class="hljs-string">`e`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> dept_no = e.dept_no</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2332">Note that the example above be achieved more easily using the <a href="#Builder-as">as</a> method.</p>
      <pre class="display" data-reactid="2333"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2334"><span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> subcolumn = knex.avg(<span class="hljs-string">'salary'</span>)
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'employee'</span>)
.whereRaw(<span class="hljs-string">'dept_no = e.dept_no'</span>)
.as(<span class="hljs-string">'avg_sal_dept'</span>);

knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'e.lastname'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'e.salary'</span>, subcolumn)
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'employee as e'</span>)
.whereRaw(<span class="hljs-string">'dept_no = e.dept_no'</span>)</code><br data-reactid="2335">
       <!-- react-text: 2336 -->Outputs:
       <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2337"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2338"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> <span class="hljs-string">`e`</span>.<span class="hljs-string">`lastname`</span>, <span class="hljs-string">`e`</span>.<span class="hljs-string">`salary`</span>, (<span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">avg</span>(<span class="hljs-string">`salary`</span>) <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`employee`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> dept_no = e.dept_no) <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> <span class="hljs-string">`avg_sal_dept`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`employee`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">as</span> <span class="hljs-string">`e`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> dept_no = e.dept_no</code></pre>
     </div>
     <div id="Utility" data-reactid="2339">
      <h2 id="Utility" data-reactid="2340">Utility</h2>
      <p data-reactid="2341">A collection of utilities that the knex library provides for convenience.</p>
      <h3 id="Utility-BatchInsert" data-reactid="2342">Batch Insert</h3>
      <div data-reactid="2343">
       <p data-reactid="2344">The <code>batchInsert</code> utility will insert a batch of rows wrapped inside a transaction <em>(which is automatically created unless explicitly given a transaction using <a href="#Builder-transacting">transacting</a>)</em>, at a given <code>chunkSize</code>.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2345">It's primarily designed to be used when you have thousands of rows to insert into a table.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2346">By default, the <code>chunkSize</code> is set to 1000.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2347">BatchInsert also allows for <a href="#Builder-returning">returning values</a> and supplying transactions using <a href="#Builder-transacting">transacting</a>.</p>
      </div>
      <pre data-reactid="2348"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2349"><span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> rows = [{...}, {...}];
<span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> chunkSize = <span class="hljs-number">30</span>;
knex.batchInsert(<span class="hljs-string">'TableName'</span>, rows, chunkSize)
  .returning(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>)
  .then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">ids</span>) </span>{ ... })
  .catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{ ... });

knex.transaction(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">tr</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> knex.batchInsert(<span class="hljs-string">'TableName'</span>, rows, chunkSize)
    .transacting(tr)
  })
  .then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{ ... })
  .catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{ ... });</code></pre>
     </div>
     <div id="Interfaces" data-reactid="2350">
      <h2 id="Interfaces" data-reactid="2351">Interfaces</h2>
      <p data-reactid="2352">Knex.js provides several options to deal with query output. The following methods are present on the query builder, schema builder, and the raw builder:</p>
      <h3 id="Interfaces-Promises" data-reactid="2353">Promises</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2354"><a href="https://github.com/petkaantonov/bluebird#what-are-promises-and-why-should-i-use-them">Promises</a> are the preferred way of dealing with queries in knex, as they allow you to return values from a fulfillment handler, which in turn become the value of the promise. The main benefit of promises are the ability to catch thrown errors without crashing the node app, making your code behave like a <strong>.try / .catch / .finally</strong> in synchronous code.</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2355"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2356">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>)
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.where(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'&gt;'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">20</span>)
.andWhere(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'&lt;'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">200</span>)
.limit(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>)
.offset(x)
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">rows</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> _.pluck(rows, <span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>);
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">names</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'nicknames'</span>).whereIn(<span class="hljs-string">'nickname'</span>, names);
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">rows</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.log(rows);
})
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(error)
});</code></pre>
      <div id="Interfaces-then" data-reactid="2357">
       <b data-reactid="2358">then</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2359 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2360">.then(onFulfilled, [onRejected])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2361">Coerces the current query builder chain into a promise state, accepting the resolve and reject handlers as specified by the Promises/A+ spec. As stated in the spec, more than one call to the then method for the current query chain will resolve with the same value, in the order they were called; the query will not be executed multiple times.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2362"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2363">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>)
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.where({<span class="hljs-attr">name</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Tim'</span>})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">rows</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> knex.insert({<span class="hljs-attr">user_id</span>: rows[<span class="hljs-number">0</span>].id, <span class="hljs-attr">name</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Test'</span>}, <span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>).into(<span class="hljs-string">'accounts'</span>);
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">id</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.log(<span class="hljs-string">'Inserted Account '</span> + id);
})
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(error); });</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-catch" data-reactid="2364">
       <b data-reactid="2365">catch</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2366 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2367">.catch(onRejected)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2368">Coerces the current query builder into a promise state, catching any error thrown by the query, the same as calling .then(null, onRejected).</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2369"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2370"><span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> knex.insert({<span class="hljs-attr">id</span>: <span class="hljs-number">1</span>, <span class="hljs-attr">name</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'Test'</span>}, <span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>)
.into(<span class="hljs-string">'accounts'</span>)
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(error);
}).then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>)
    .from(<span class="hljs-string">'accounts'</span>)
    .where(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">1</span>);
}).then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">rows</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.log(rows[<span class="hljs-number">0</span>]);
})
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(error);
});</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-tap" data-reactid="2371">
       <b data-reactid="2372">tap</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2373 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2374">.tap(sideEffectHandler)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2375">Executes side effects on the resolved response, ultimately returning a promise that fulfills with the original value. A thrown error or rejected promise will cause the promise to transition into a rejected state.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2376"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2377"><span class="hljs-comment">// Using only .then()</span>
query.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">x</span>) </span>{
  doSideEffectsHere(x);
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> x;
});

<span class="hljs-comment">// Using .tap()</span>
promise.tap(doSideEffectsHere);</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-map" data-reactid="2378">
       <b data-reactid="2379">map</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2380 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2381">.map(mapper)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2382">A passthrough to Bluebird's map implementation with the result set.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2383"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2384">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).limit(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>).map(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">row</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> row.name;
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">names</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.log(names); })
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">e</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(e); });</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-reduce" data-reactid="2385">
       <b data-reactid="2386">reduce</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2387 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2388">.reduce(reducer, [initialValue])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2389">A passthrough to Bluebird's reduce implementation with the result set.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2390"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2391">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).limit(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>).reduce(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">memo, row</span>) </span>{
  memo.names.push(row.name);
  memo.count++;
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> memo;
}, {<span class="hljs-attr">count</span>: <span class="hljs-number">0</span>, <span class="hljs-attr">names</span>: []})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">obj</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.log(obj); })
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">e</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(e); });</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-bind" data-reactid="2392">
       <b data-reactid="2393">bind</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2394 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2395">.bind(context)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2396">A passthrough to Bluebird's bind method which sets the context value (this) for the returned promise.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2397"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2398">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.limit(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>)
.bind(<span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>)
.then(<span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.log)
.catch(<span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error)</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-return" data-reactid="2399">
       <b data-reactid="2400">return</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2401 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2402">.return(value)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2403">Shorthand for calling .then(function() { return value }).</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2404"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2405"><span class="hljs-comment">// Without return:</span>
knex.insert(values).into(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
  .then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{
    <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> {<span class="hljs-attr">inserted</span>: <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>};
  });

knex.insert(values).into(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).return({<span class="hljs-attr">inserted</span>: <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>});</code></pre>
      </div>
      <h3 id="Interfaces-Callbacks" data-reactid="2406">Callbacks</h3>
      <div id="Interfaces-asCallback" data-reactid="2407">
       <b data-reactid="2408">asCallback</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2409 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2410">.asCallback(callback)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2411">If you'd prefer a callback interface over promises, the asCallback function accepts a standard node style callback for executing the query chain. Note that as with the then method, subsequent calls to the same query chain will return the same result.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2412"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2413">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.where(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'&gt;'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">20</span>)
.andWhere(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>, <span class="hljs-string">'&lt;'</span>, <span class="hljs-number">200</span>)
.limit(<span class="hljs-number">10</span>)
.offset(x)
.asCallback(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">err, rows</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (err) <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(err);
  knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'id'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'nicknames'</span>)
    .whereIn(<span class="hljs-string">'nickname'</span>, _.pluck(rows, <span class="hljs-string">'name'</span>))
    .asCallback(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">err, rows</span>) </span>{
      <span class="hljs-keyword">if</span> (err) <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(err);
      <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.log(rows);
    });
});</code></pre>
      </div>
      <h3 id="Interfaces-Streams" data-reactid="2414">Streams</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2415">Streams are a powerful way of piping data through as it comes in, rather than all at once. You can read more about streams <a href="https://github.com/substack/stream-handbook">here at substack's stream handbook</a>. See the following for example uses of stream &amp; pipe. If you wish to use streams with PostgreSQL, you must also install the <a href="https://github.com/brianc/node-pg-query-stream">pg-query-stream</a> module. On an HTTP server, make sure to <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/wiki/Manually-Closing-Streams">manually close your streams</a> if a request is aborted.</p>
      <div id="Interfaces-stream" data-reactid="2416">
       <b data-reactid="2417">stream</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2418 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2419">.stream([options], [callback])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2420">If called with a callback, the callback is passed the stream and a promise is returned. Otherwise, the readable stream is returned.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2421"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2422"><span class="hljs-comment">// Retrieve the stream:</span>
<span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> stream = knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).stream();
stream.pipe(writableStream);

<span class="hljs-comment">// With options:</span>
<span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> stream = knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).stream({<span class="hljs-attr">highWaterMark</span>: <span class="hljs-number">5</span>});
stream.pipe(writableStream);

<span class="hljs-comment">// Use as a promise:</span>
<span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> stream = knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
  .where(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'id = ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>]))
  .stream(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">stream</span>) </span>{
    stream.pipe(writableStream);
  })
  .then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-comment">// ... })</span>
  .catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">e</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-built_in">console</span>.error(e); });</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-pipe" data-reactid="2423">
       <b data-reactid="2424">pipe</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2425 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2426">.pipe(writableStream)</code>
       <p data-reactid="2427">Pipe a stream for the current query to a writableStream.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2428"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2429"><span class="hljs-keyword">var</span> stream = knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).pipe(writableStream);</code></pre>
      </div>
      <h3 id="Interfaces-Events" data-reactid="2430">Events</h3>
      <div id="Interfaces-query" data-reactid="2431">
       <b data-reactid="2432">query</b>
       <p data-reactid="2433">A query event is fired just before a query takes place, providing data about the query, including the connection's __cid property and any other information about the query as described in toSQL. Useful for logging all queries throughout your application.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2434"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2435">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>)
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.on(<span class="hljs-string">'query'</span>, <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">data</span>) </span>{
  app.log(data);
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-comment">// ...</span>
});</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-query-error" data-reactid="2436">
       <b data-reactid="2437">query-error</b>
       <p data-reactid="2438">A query-error event is fired when an error occurs when running a query, providing the error object and data about the query, including the connection's __cid property and any other information about the query as described in toSQL. Useful for logging all query errors throughout your application.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2439"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2440">knex.select([<span class="hljs-string">'NonExistentColumn'</span>])
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.on(<span class="hljs-string">'query-error'</span>, <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error, obj</span>) </span>{
  app.log(error);
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-comment">// ... })</span>
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-comment">// Same error object as the query-error event provides.</span>
});</code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-query-response" data-reactid="2441">
       <b data-reactid="2442">query-response</b>
       <p data-reactid="2443">A query-response event is fired when a successful query has been run, providing the response of the query and data about the query, including the connection's __cid property and any other information about the query as described in toSQL, and finally the query builder used for the query.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2444"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2445">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>)
.from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>)
.on(<span class="hljs-string">'query-response'</span>, <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">response, obj, builder</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-comment">// ...</span>
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">response</span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-comment">// Same response as the emitted event</span>
})
.catch(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">error</span>) </span>{ });</code></pre>
      </div>
      <h3 id="Interfaces-Other" data-reactid="2446">Other</h3>
      <div id="Interfaces-toString" data-reactid="2447">
       <b data-reactid="2448">toString</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2449 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2450">.toString()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2451">Returns an array of query strings filled out with the correct values based on bindings, etc. Useful for debugging.</p>
       <pre class="display" data-reactid="2452"><code class="js hljs" data-reactid="2453">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).where(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'id = ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>])).toString()</code><br data-reactid="2454">
        <!-- react-text: 2455 -->Outputs:
        <!-- /react-text --><br data-reactid="2456"><code class="sql hljs" data-reactid="2457"><span class="hljs-keyword">select</span> * <span class="hljs-keyword">from</span> <span class="hljs-string">`users`</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">where</span> <span class="hljs-keyword">id</span> = <span class="hljs-number">1</span></code></pre>
      </div>
      <div id="Interfaces-toSQL" data-reactid="2458">
       <b data-reactid="2459">toSQL</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2460 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2461">.toSQL()</code>
       <p data-reactid="2462">Returns an array of query strings filled out with the correct values based on bindings, etc. Useful for debugging.</p>
       <pre data-reactid="2463"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2464">knex.select(<span class="hljs-string">'*'</span>).from(<span class="hljs-string">'users'</span>).where(knex.raw(<span class="hljs-string">'id = ?'</span>, [<span class="hljs-number">1</span>])).toSQL()

<span class="hljs-comment">// Ouputs: { bindings: [1], method: 'select', sql: 'select * from "users" where id = ?', options: undefined, }</span></code></pre>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div id="Migrations" data-reactid="2465">
      <h2 id="Migrations" data-reactid="2466">Migrations</h2>
      <p data-reactid="2467">Migrations allow for you to define sets of schema changes so upgrading a database is a breeze.</p>
      <h3 id="Migrations-CLI" data-reactid="2468">Migration CLI</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2469">The migration CLI is bundled with the knex install, and is driven by the <a href="https://github.com/tkellen/node-liftoff">node-liftoff</a> module. To install globally, run:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2470"><code data-reactid="2471">$ npm install knex -g</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2472">Migrations use a <strong>knexfile</strong>, which specify various configuration settings for the module. To create a new knexfile, run the following:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2473"><code data-reactid="2474">$ knex init

# or for .coffee

$ knex init -x coffee</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2475">will create a sample knexfile.js - the file which contains our various database configurations. Once you have a knexfile.js, you can use the migration tool to create migration files to the specified directory (default migrations). Creating new migration files can be achieved by running:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2476"><code data-reactid="2477">$ knex migrate:make migration_name</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2478">Once you have finished writing the migrations, you can update the database matching your <code>NODE_ENV</code> by running:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2479"><code data-reactid="2480">$ knex migrate:latest</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2481">You can also pass the <code>--env</code> flag or set <code>NODE_ENV</code> to select an alternative environment:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2482"><code data-reactid="2483">$ knex migrate:latest --env production

# or

$ NODE_ENV=production knex migrate:latest</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2484">To rollback the last batch of migrations:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2485"><code data-reactid="2486">$ knex migrate:rollback</code></pre>
      <h2 id="Seeds" data-reactid="2487">Seed files</h2>
      <p data-reactid="2488">Seed files allow you to populate your database with test or seed data independent of your migration files.</p>
      <h3 id="Seeds-CLI" data-reactid="2489">Seed CLI</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2490">To create a seed file, run:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2491"><code data-reactid="2492">$ knex seed:make seed_name</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2493">Seed files are created in the directory specified in your knexfile.js for the current environment. A sample seed configuration looks like:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2494"><code data-reactid="2495">development: {
  client: ...,
  connection: { ... },
  seeds: {
      directory: './seeds/dev'
  }
}</code></pre>
      <div data-reactid="2496">
       <p data-reactid="2497">If no <code>seeds.directory</code> is defined, files are created in <code>./seeds</code>. Note that the seed directory needs to be a relative path. Absolute paths are not supported (nor is it good practice).</p>
       <p data-reactid="2498">To run seed files, execute:</p>
      </div>
      <pre data-reactid="2499"><code data-reactid="2500">$ knex seed:run</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2501">Seed files are executed in alphabetical order. Unlike migrations, <em>every</em> seed file will be executed when you run the command. You should design your seed files to reset tables as needed before inserting data.</p>
      <h3 id="knexfile" data-reactid="2502">knexfile.js</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2503">A knexfile.js or knexfile.coffee generally contains all of the configuration for your database. It can optionally provide different configuration for different environments. You may pass a <code>--knexfile</code> option to any of the command line statements to specify an alternate path to your knexfile.</p>
      <h4 data-reactid="2504">Basic configuration:</h4>
      <pre data-reactid="2505"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2506"><span class="hljs-built_in">module</span>.exports = {
  <span class="hljs-attr">client</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'pg'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">connection</span>: process.env.DATABASE_URL || { <span class="hljs-attr">user</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'me'</span>, <span class="hljs-attr">database</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'my_app'</span> }
};</code></pre>
      <h4 data-reactid="2507">Environment configuration:</h4>
      <pre data-reactid="2508"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2509"><span class="hljs-built_in">module</span>.exports = {
  <span class="hljs-attr">development</span>: {
    <span class="hljs-attr">client</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'pg'</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">connection</span>: { <span class="hljs-attr">user</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'me'</span>, <span class="hljs-attr">database</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'my_app'</span> }
  },
  <span class="hljs-attr">production</span>: { <span class="hljs-attr">client</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'pg'</span>, <span class="hljs-attr">connection</span>: process.env.DATABASE_URL }
};</code></pre>
      <h4 data-reactid="2510">Custom migration:</h4>
      <p data-reactid="2511">You may provide a custom migration stub to be used in place of the default option.</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2512"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2513"><span class="hljs-built_in">module</span>.exports = {
  <span class="hljs-attr">client</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'pg'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">migration</span>: {
    <span class="hljs-attr">stub</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'migration.stub'</span>
  }
};</code></pre>
      <h3 id="Migrations-API" data-reactid="2514">Migration API</h3>
      <div data-reactid="2515">
       <p data-reactid="2516"><code>knex.migrate</code> is the class utilized by the knex migrations cli.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2517">Each method takes an optional <code>config</code> object, which may specify the following properties:</p>
      </div>
      <ul data-reactid="2518">
       <li data-reactid="2519"><code>directory</code>: a relative path to the directory containing the migration files (default <code>./migrations</code>)</li>
       <li data-reactid="2520"><code>extension</code>: the file extension used for the generated migration files (default <code>js</code>)</li>
       <li data-reactid="2521"><code>tableName</code>: the table name used for storing the migration state (default <code>knex_migrations</code>)</li>
       <li data-reactid="2522"><code>disableTransactions</code>: don't run migrations inside transactions (default <code>false</code>)</li>
      </ul>
      <h4 id="Migrations-API-transactions" data-reactid="2523">Transactions in migrations</h4>
      <p data-reactid="2524">By default, each migration is run inside a transaction. Whenever needed, one can disable transactions for all migrations via the common migration config option <code>config.disableTransactions</code> or per-migration, via exposing a boolean property <code>config.transaction</code> from a migration file:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2525"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2526">exports.up = <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">knex, Promise</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-comment">/* ... */</span> };

exports.down = <span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params">knex, Promise</span>) </span>{ <span class="hljs-comment">/* ... */</span> };

exports.config = { <span class="hljs-attr">transaction</span>: <span class="hljs-literal">false</span> };</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2527">The same config property can be used for enabling transaction per-migration in case the common configuration has <code>disableTransactions: true</code>.</p>
      <div id="Migrations-make" data-reactid="2528">
       <b data-reactid="2529">make</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2530 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2531">knex.migrate.make(name, [config])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2532">Creates a new migration, with the name of the migration being added.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Migrations-latest" data-reactid="2533">
       <b data-reactid="2534">latest</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2535 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2536">knex.migrate.latest([config])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2537">Runs all migrations that have not yet been run.</p>
      </div>
      <p data-reactid="2538">If you need to run something only after all migrations have finished their execution, you can do something like this:</p>
      <pre data-reactid="2539"><code class="hljs js" data-reactid="2540">knex.migrate.latest()
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-keyword">return</span> knex.seed.run();
})
.then(<span class="hljs-function"><span class="hljs-keyword">function</span>(<span class="hljs-params"></span>) </span>{
  <span class="hljs-comment">// migrations are finished</span>
});</code></pre>
      <div id="Migrations-rollback" data-reactid="2541">
       <b data-reactid="2542">rollback</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2543 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2544">knex.migrate.rollback([config])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2545">Rolls back the latest migration group.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Migrations-currentVersion" data-reactid="2546">
       <b data-reactid="2547">currentVersion</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2548 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2549">knex.migrate.currentVersion([config])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2550">Retrieves and returns the current migration version, as a promise. If there aren't any migrations run yet, returns "none" as the value for the currentVersion.</p>
      </div>
      <h3 id="Notes-about-locks" data-reactid="2551">Notes about locks</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2552">A lock system is there to prevent multiple processes from running the same migration batch in the same time. When a batch of migrations is about to be run, the migration system first tries to get a lock using a <code>SELECT ... FOR UPDATE</code> statement (preventing race conditions from happening). If it can get a lock, the migration batch will run. If it can't, it will wait until the lock is released.</p>
      <p data-reactid="2553">Please note that if your process unfortunately crashes, the lock will have to be <em>manually</em> removed in order to let migrations run again. The locks are saved in a table called "<code>tableName</code>_lock"; it has single one column called <code>is_locked</code> that you need to set to <code>0</code> in order to release the lock.</p>
     </div>
     <div id="Seeds" data-reactid="2554">
      <h3 id="Seeds-API" data-reactid="2555">Seed API</h3>
      <p data-reactid="2556"><code>knex.seed</code> is the class utilized by the knex seed CLI. Each method takes an optional <code>config</code> object, which may specify the relative <code>directory</code> for the migrations.</p>
      <div id="Seeds-make" data-reactid="2557">
       <b data-reactid="2558">make</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2559 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2560">knex.seed.make(name, [config])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2561">Creates a new seed file, with the name of the seed file being added.</p>
      </div>
      <div id="Seeds-run" data-reactid="2562">
       <b data-reactid="2563">run</b>
       <!-- react-text: 2564 --> — 
       <!-- /react-text -->
       <code data-reactid="2565">knex.seed.run([config])</code>
       <p data-reactid="2566">Runs all seed files for the current environment.</p>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div id="Support" data-reactid="2567">
      <h2 id="support" data-reactid="2568">Support</h2>
      <p data-reactid="2569">Have questions about the library? Come join us in the <a href="http://webchat.freenode.net/?channels=bookshelf">#bookshelf freenode IRC</a> channel for support on knex.js and <a href="http://bookshelfjs.org">bookshelf.js</a>, or post an issue on <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/tagged/knex.js">Stack Overflow</a> or in the GitHub <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues">issue tracker</a>.</p>
     </div>
     <div id="Faq" data-reactid="2570">
      <h2 id="faq" data-reactid="2571">F.A.Q.</h2>
      <div data-reactid="2572">
       <p data-reactid="2573"><strong>How do I help contribute?</strong><br>Glad you ask! Pull requests, or feature requests, though not always implemented, are a great way to help make Knex even better than it is now. If you're looking for something specific to help out with, there's a number of unit tests that aren't implemented yet, the library could never have too many of those. If you want to submit a fix or feature, take a look at the <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/blob/master/CONTRIBUTING.md">Contributing</a> readme in the Github and go ahead and open a ticket.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2574"><strong>How do I debug?</strong><br>Knex is beginning to make use of the <a href="https://github.com/visionmedia/debug">debug</a> module internally, so you can set the <code>DEBUG</code> environment variable to <code>knex:*</code> to see all debugging, or select individual namespaces <code>DEBUG=knex:query,knex:tx</code> to constrain a bit.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2575">If you pass <code>{debug: true}</code> as one of the options in your initialize settings, you can see all of the query calls being made. Sometimes you need to dive a bit further into the various calls and see what all is going on behind the scenes. I'd recommend <a href="https://github.com/dannycoates/node-inspector">node-inspector</a>, which allows you to debug code with <code>debugger</code> statements like you would in the browser.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2576">At the start of your application code will catch any errors not otherwise caught in the normal promise chain handlers, which is very helpful in debugging.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2577"><strong>How do I run the test suite?</strong><br>The test suite looks for an environment variable called <code>KNEX_TEST</code> for the path to the database configuration. If you run the following command:</p>
      </div>
      <pre data-reactid="2578"><code data-reactid="2579">$ export KNEX_TEST='/path/to/your/knex_config.js'
$ npm test</code></pre>
      <div data-reactid="2580">
       <p data-reactid="2581">replacing with the path to your config file, and the config file is valid, the test suite should run properly.</p>
       <p data-reactid="2582"><strong>My tests are failing because slow DB connection and short test timeouts! How to extend test timeouts?</strong><br>Sometimes, e.g. when running CI on travis, test suite's default timeout of 5 seconds might be too short. In such cases an alternative test timeout value in milliseconds can be specified using the <code>KNEX_TEST_TIMEOUT</code> environment variable.</p>
      </div>
      <pre data-reactid="2583"><code data-reactid="2584">$ export KNEX_TEST_TIMEOUT=30000
$ npm test</code></pre>
      <p data-reactid="2585"><strong>Can I use Knex outside of Node.js</strong><br>Yes. While the WebSQL spec is deprecated, there is still an adapter that provides support. You will need to use a build tool like browserify or webpack for a browser build.</p>
     </div>

        <div data-reactid="2942">
         <b class="header" data-reactid="2943">0.8.0</b>
         <!-- react-text: 2944 --> — 
         <!-- /react-text -->
         <small data-reactid="2945"><i data-reactid="2946">Apr 30, 2015</i></small>
         <br data-reactid="2947">
         <b data-reactid="2948">New Features:</b>
         <ul data-reactid="2949">
          <li data-reactid="2950">Fixes several major outstanding bugs with the connection pool, switching to <a href="https://github.com/myndzi/pool2">Pool2</a> in place of generic-pool-redux</li>
          <li data-reactid="2951">strong-oracle module support</li>
          <li data-reactid="2952">Nested transactions automatically become savepoints, with <code>commit</code> &amp; <code>rollback</code> releasing or rolling back the current savepoint.</li>
          <li data-reactid="2953">Database seed file support, <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/391">#391</a></li>
          <li data-reactid="2954">Improved support for sub-raw queries within raw statements</li>
          <li data-reactid="2955">Migrations are now wrapped in transactions where possible</li>
          <li data-reactid="2956">Subqueries supported in insert statements, <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/627">#627</a></li>
          <li data-reactid="2957">Support for nested having, <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/572">#572</a></li>
          <li data-reactid="2958">Support object syntax for joins, similar to "where" <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/743">#743</a></li>
         </ul>
         <b data-reactid="2959">Major Changes:</b>
         <ul data-reactid="2960">
          <li data-reactid="2961">Transactions are immediately invoked as A+ promises, <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/470">#470</a> (this is a feature and should not actually break anything in practice)</li>
          <li data-reactid="2962">Heavy refactoring internal APIs (public APIs should not be affected)</li>
         </ul>
         <b data-reactid="2963">"Other Changes:</b>
         <ul data-reactid="2964">
          <li data-reactid="2965">Allow mysql2 to use non-default port, <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/588">#588</a></li>
          <li data-reactid="2966">Support creating &amp; dropping extensions in PostgreSQL, <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/540">#540</a></li>
          <li data-reactid="2967">CLI support for knexfiles that do not provide environment keys, <a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/527">#527</a></li>
          <li data-reactid="2968">Added sqlite3 dialect version of whereRaw/andWhereRaw (<a href="https://github.com/tgriesser/knex/issues/477">#477</a>)</li>
         </ul>
        </div>
